    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5161127777895631771"><br/>In her <i>New York Times </i>bestselling <b>Outlander</b><i> </i>novels, Diana Gabaldon introduced millions of readers to a dazzling world of history and adventure — a world of vibrant settings and utterly unforgettable characters. Now one of these characters, Major Lord John Grey, opens the door to his own part of this world — eighteenth-century London, a seething anthill of nobility and rabb</span>
  <span id="freeText5161127777895631771" style="display:none"><br />In her <i>New York Times </i>bestselling <b>Outlander</b><i> </i>novels, Diana Gabaldon introduced millions of readers to a dazzling world of history and adventure — a world of vibrant settings and utterly unforgettable characters. Now one of these characters, Major Lord John Grey, opens the door to his own part of this world — eighteenth-century London, a seething anthill of nobility and rabble peopled by soldiers and spies, whores and dukes. Great Britain is battling France for supremacy on three continents — and life is good for a soldier.<br /><br />The year is 1757. On a clear morning in mid-June, Lord John Grey emerges from London’s Beefsteak Club, his mind in turmoil. A nobleman and a high-ranking officer in His Majesty’s Army, Grey has just witnessed something shocking. But his efforts to avoid a scandal that might destroy his family are interrupted by something still more urgent: the Crown appoints him to investigate the brutal murder of a comrade in arms, who may have been a traitor.<br /><br />Obliged to pursue two inquiries at once, Major Grey finds himself ensnared in a web of treachery and betrayal that touches every stratum of English society — and threatens all he holds dear. From the bawdy houses of London’s night-world to the stately drawing rooms of the nobility, and from the blood of a murdered corpse to the thundering seas ruled by the majestic fleet of the East India Company, Lord John pursues the elusive trails of a vanishing footman and a woman in green velvet, who may hold the key to everything — or nothing.<br /><br />The early days of the Seven Years War come brilliantly to life in this historical mystery by an author whose unique and compelling storytelling has engrossed millions of readers worldwide.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5161127777895631771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">this is the order as indicated by the author:<br/><br/>•Lord John and the Hellfire Club, a short story.<br/>•LORD JOHN AND THE PRIVATE MATTER, a novel.<br/>•Lord John and<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">this is the order as indicated by the author:<br /><br />•Lord John and the Hellfire Club, a short story.<br />•LORD JOHN AND THE PRIVATE MATTER, a novel.<br />•Lord John and the Succubus a novella,<br />•LORD JOHN AND THE BROTHERHOOD OF THE BLADE, a novel.<br />•Lord John and the Haunted Soldier, a novella.<br />•Lord John and the Custom of the Army, a novella.<br />•THE SCOTTISH PRISONER, a novel.<br />•Lord John and the Plague of Zombies.<br /><br />Lord John was mentioned in previous novels of outlanders as well but only as a minor character.<br /><br />I hope you find this useful<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes. I read on Diana Gabaldon's web page that the Lord John series may be read in any order and separate from the Outlander books. I've read all of th<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes. I read on Diana Gabaldon's web page that the Lord John series may be read in any order and separate from the Outlander books. I've read all of the Outlander series and I'm now reading all of these. Just finished Lord John and the Private Matter which was very good. Enjoy!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_82490719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82490719" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82490719?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=mysteries-thrillers-horror">mysteries-thrillers-horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82490719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18029684270993802063">Like many other "Outlander" fans, I've been reluctant to even attempt to read this second Gabaldon series which centers on a secondary gay character first introduced in "Dragonfly in Amber." I was discouraged not only by the average Goodreads rating of 3.35, but by the sheer memory of THE homosexual encounter in "Outlander." I simply didn't feel like going through the same pain and suffering again. But then the 7th book came out ("An Echo in the Bone") and everybody was saying that you had to ha</span>
  <span id="freeText18029684270993802063" style="display:none">Like many other "Outlander" fans, I've been reluctant to even attempt to read this second Gabaldon series which centers on a secondary gay character first introduced in "Dragonfly in Amber." I was discouraged not only by the average Goodreads rating of 3.35, but by the sheer memory of THE homosexual encounter in "Outlander." I simply didn't feel like going through the same pain and suffering again. But then the 7th book came out ("An Echo in the Bone") and everybody was saying that you had to have read Lord John books to really get into the story. Of course, in this case, I simply had to at least try to read these books to be sufficiently prepared for future series installments. <br /><br />Well, I am pleased to say that I enjoyed "Lord John and the Private Matter" very much. I understand however where the low ratings came from. This book is nothing like Outlander books. They are different in genre, in size, even in vocabulary. This Lord John book is a historical mystery with a lot of old-fashioned sleuthing, unlike smutty romance/adventure type Outlander books are. What remains the same in both series however is the high quality of writing, fantastic characterization and smartly presented historical details.<br /><br />There is no passionate love story (not even a gay one) in "Lord John and the Private Matter," but it is filled with political intrigues and discussions of military affairs, and I enjoyed every bit of it. The subject of homosexuality is presented throughout the story: not only is it always in the back of Lord John' mind, but we also have to follow our protagonist sleuthing through brothels, male secret rendezvous houses and chasing transvestites. Needless to say, it all was new to me, because honestly I know very little about gay life style and especially that in 18th century London. <br /><br />As for Lord John himself and his personal life, Gabaldon managed to make me appreciate this man of honor and feel a lot of compassion for his plight, because if nothing else he is a lonely man who among other things is forced to keep an important part of self hidden at all times, because his "preference" can simply have him executed. <br /><br />What else is there to say? Only that I thoroughly enjoyed this well-written mystery which started as a quest to find out if Lord John's future cousin-in-law had syphilis and ended with him solving two murders and uncovering a spy against England. I am definitely reading the rest of the books in this series. <br /><br />P.S. Just a heads-up, there was one man/man sex scene involving Lord John, but it wasn't at all graphic, although you do know what's going on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18029684270993802063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_28476912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28476912" />
    <a title="Marcie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/688404-marcie"><img alt="Marcie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311271640p2/688404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28476912?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marcie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marcie" href="/user/show/688404-marcie">Marcie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28476912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8792775213141600611">I resisted reading any Lord John stories for a very long time, despite being a huge Gabaldon fan. I just couldn't get behind a gay lead, didn't understand the appeal or potential of this character. I didn't get it, without even trying it. Recently I saw Gabaldon at a sci-fi convention, and to get in the mood for it, I dug out this book, which I had snagged at a library discard sale for a buck or so.<br/><br/>I get it now. He's delightful. Imagine a slight, blonde, aristocratic, rich, devastatingly smart a</span>
  <span id="freeText8792775213141600611" style="display:none">I resisted reading any Lord John stories for a very long time, despite being a huge Gabaldon fan. I just couldn't get behind a gay lead, didn't understand the appeal or potential of this character. I didn't get it, without even trying it. Recently I saw Gabaldon at a sci-fi convention, and to get in the mood for it, I dug out this book, which I had snagged at a library discard sale for a buck or so.<br /><br />I get it now. He's delightful. Imagine a slight, blonde, aristocratic, rich, devastatingly smart and witty professional soldier, a Major in Her Majesty's service in 1757, who finds himself up to his impeccable chin in murder, mayhem, and mystery. It's like both William Powell and Myrna Loy (of the old Thin Man movies) rolled into one character, with a touch of television's Monk thrown in.<br /><br />Fun! He is so particular about his clothes and appearance and there's this running subconscious dialogue interspersed with the bigger external picture unfolding in his head that goes something like this: "Ah, ha, so the Scanlons have flown the coop which must be a big clue!...and I seem to have lost a button on my waistcoat." He is always picking at a loose thread, flicking lint on his shoulder, noticing every detail around him. You can just picture his futzing.<br /><br />He is also very adept at the dry one-word reply – indubiously, quite, likely, mayhaps. I really enjoyed it, and should have had more trust in her unbelievable writing talent. Interestingly, the one "sex scene" involving Lord John was very well-done, compelling, and poignant and definitely germane to the story. He simply loses himself, tastefully fades to black, and whispers "Pretend…I am not here." And I truly believe he wishes it were so.<br /><br />Contrast his fastidious personal quirks with his loathsome outward duty, and you've got a very entertaining setup. He is the only one in the room who will sink his fingers into the mushy scalp of a corpse for a clue or carry around the reeking blood-soaked remnant of a garment with which to confront the bad guy. Then there's his fiercely protective little side kick, a ragamuffin English boy who follows him around and insists that he be his valet. The little boy is just as comical, giving "me lord" the steely eye as he makes him drink MANY egg whites as a poison antidote and tries to mend his endlessly destroyed clothes.<br /><br />I can't wait to read more Lord John. Undoubtedly.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8792775213141600611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_481866415" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/481866415" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/481866415?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer481866415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12233024511696393925">Gabaldon reacquaints readers with Lord John Grey. In Grey's first full-length novel set in 18th century London, nobility and the rabble cross paths, while whores and dukes solicit one another. Grey is an active soldier, living the good life, as Great Britain fends off France on three continents. Emerging from his club one June morning in 1757, Grey possesses a secret that may permanently damage his family, should the wrong person learn of its nature. As this plagues him, the Crown sends him to i</span>
  <span id="freeText12233024511696393925" style="display:none">Gabaldon reacquaints readers with Lord John Grey. In Grey's first full-length novel set in 18th century London, nobility and the rabble cross paths, while whores and dukes solicit one another. Grey is an active soldier, living the good life, as Great Britain fends off France on three continents. Emerging from his club one June morning in 1757, Grey possesses a secret that may permanently damage his family, should the wrong person learn of its nature. As this plagues him, the Crown sends him to investigate the murder of a fellow soldier, who may have had treasonous intentions, opening up the suspect pool exponentially. Working on two investigations simultaneously, Grey and his newly hired valet, Tom Byrd, seek to bring matters to a head without alerting too many individuals. The more they investigate, on both counts, the more sordid things become. Grey must follow a poxed person's proclivities (try saying that five times!) in order to help his own family, but ends up solving both cases utilising his sharp logic while traversing the seas in search of a woman in green velvet, who may hold the key to everything, or prove yet another wasted journey away from Mother England. This novel set in the early days of the Seven Years War and post-Jamie Fraser first encounters offers the reader much historical insight while also setting the scene to further the story told briefly in Gabaldon's VOYAGER.<br /><br />In his role as military Sherlock Holmes, Grey seeks to close all doors and solve the cases put before him without rocking the proverbial boat. This can prove highly difficult, when 18th century London is the setting, as anything goes and usually ends up happening. Grey uses his sleuthing abilities to show his multi-dimensional character seen already in VOYAGER and a novella, which is likely expanded in the rest of the LJG collection. Gabaldon has such a firm handle on all her characters that the attentive reader may look for more crossovers or crumbs mentioned in one series and resolved in the other. Just when I wanted to listen and enjoy, I have to be on my toes!<br /><br />Kudos, Madam Gabaldon for this wonderful tale, full of intrigue and sleuthing. I look forward to learning more and seeing how one Jamie Fraser plays a keener role in the larger story. <br /><br />Like/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12233024511696393925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

He is entrusted with searching for the answers to two murders and to a spy selling secrets. Lord John discovers a man by the name of O'Connell may have sold military secrets to an enemy spy.   <span id="freeText11856371901660644503" style="display:none"><strong>Lord John Grey</strong><br /><br />Lord John Grey is a major in His Majesty's army . He is entrusted with searching for the answers to two murders and to a spy selling secrets. Lord John discovers a man by the name of O'Connell may have sold military secrets to an enemy spy. There are plenty of clues to all three crimes, but they're not coming together in a cohesive answer. Perhaps they are all separate crimes and not tied together. Will Lord John Grey discover the answers before it's too late?<br /><br />Diana Gabaldon has written another winner. Lord John Grey is a character from the Outlander series. He, along with the secondary characters, are a delight to make the acquaintance of. We come to fully understand Lord John's character through dialogue and descriptions. The plot and subplots are tightly drawn and feel feasible. The setting and description places the reader directly in the story. There is a m/m sexual scene tastefully written. I highly recommend this novel.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2602777983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11029581677672747801">4.5★s<br/>Lord John and the Private Matter is the first novel in the Lord John Grey series by popular American author, Diana Gabaldon. As he waits for his next posting, Lord John Grey, a Major in His Majesty’s 47th Regiment, learns of the death of a Sergeant well known to him. Something is off when he pays the widow a condolence visit, and his friend, Colonel Harry Quarry reveals that Sergeant O’Connell was suspected of being a spy. The man they had shadowing him has disappeared and Grey is set the t</span>
  <span id="freeText11029581677672747801" style="display:none">4.5★s<br />Lord John and the Private Matter is the first novel in the Lord John Grey series by popular American author, Diana Gabaldon. As he waits for his next posting, Lord John Grey, a Major in His Majesty’s 47th Regiment, learns of the death of a Sergeant well known to him. Something is off when he pays the widow a condolence visit, and his friend, Colonel Harry Quarry reveals that Sergeant O’Connell was suspected of being a spy. The man they had shadowing him has disappeared and Grey is set the task of investigating.<br /><br />At the same time, quite by chance, Grey comes across a disturbing fact about the Hon. Joseph Trevelyan, the prospective husband of his niece, Olivia Pearsall. As Grey makes enquiries to confirm or dismiss his concerns, he discovers more alarming details, and the boundaries between his two fields of investigation begin to blur. <br /><br />Before Grey finally learns what has transpired, he will visit a brothel and a molly house, examine two dead bodies, acquire a new valet, suffer mercury poisoning, encounter cross-dressers, drink quite a bit of German wine, adjudicate in a fight over a corpse, and board a ship headed for India. There are plenty of twists and turns before the exciting climax of this rather enjoyable piece of historical fiction. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11029581677672747801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_425478890" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/425478890" />
    <a title="Irina Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7664770-irina-elena"><img alt="Irina Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587303756p2/7664770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/425478890?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer2949261533205559106">Very quickly:<br/>this was a good book (kind of?), but <i>booooring</i>. I like the writing and the research is incredibly well done, with no historical info dumping, but there was one issue that I just could not get past.<br/>I read books for the plot, obviously, but just as much, if not more, for the characters. Here, we don't get to know anything about Lord John. <i>Anything</i>. The focus is on the plot, with a generous helping of colorful side characters, but basically all I feel now that I'm done with the book is</span>
  <span id="freeText2949261533205559106" style="display:none">Very quickly:<br />this was a good book (kind of?), but <i>booooring</i>. I like the writing and the research is incredibly well done, with no historical info dumping, but there was one issue that I just could not get past.<br />I read books for the plot, obviously, but just as much, if not more, for the characters. Here, we don't get to know anything about Lord John. <i>Anything</i>. The focus is on the plot, with a generous helping of colorful side characters, but basically all I feel now that I'm done with the book is a grudging curiosity towards John Grey. Of which, I repeat, I know nothing. Hector? The fuck is Hector? Where did John grow up? What about his brothers? What's his relationship with them?... and so on.<br /><br />I suppose I will read the novellas collected in Lord John and the Hand of Devils, sometime in the future.<br /><br />So. Frustrated.</span>

<div id="review_766833931" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/766833931" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/766833931?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780440241485" href="/book/show/2748563-lord-john-and-the-private-matter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=anglophilia">anglophilia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=espionage">espionage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=class-gender-race">class-gender-race</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=murder-most-foul">murder-most-foul</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=manly-men-and-their-manparts">manly-men-and-their-manparts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer766833931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2555064938604468369">I really didn’t expect to like this book as much as I did, even harboring affection for Gabaldon’s Outlander books, and especially the character of Lord John Grey, whom I find to be adorable and heartbreaking.<br/> <br/>The Lord John Grey series is a spin-off of Outlander, following Lord John Grey, a character first introduced in <i>Dragonfly in Amber</i> as a sixteen year old boy who encounters Jamie and Claire the night before the battle at Prestonpans, but he’s most prominent (at least as far as I’ve read in </span>
  <span id="freeText2555064938604468369" style="display:none">I really didn’t expect to like this book as much as I did, even harboring affection for Gabaldon’s Outlander books, and especially the character of Lord John Grey, whom I find to be adorable and heartbreaking.<br /> <br />The Lord John Grey series is a spin-off of Outlander, following Lord John Grey, a character first introduced in <i>Dragonfly in Amber</i> as a sixteen year old boy who encounters Jamie and Claire the night before the battle at Prestonpans, but he’s most prominent (at least as far as I’ve read in books 1-5) in <i>Voyager</i>, which is a book that spans twenty years. In those twenty years, Jamie and LJG meet again, and eventually become friends, although we only see select scenes of their friendship, including one in which Grey’s unrequited love for Jamie threatens to ruin said friendship. The LJG series takes place during the years covered in <i>Voyager</i>. It’s not necessary to read the Outlander series before reading this series, but the context does help, especially when LJG references his relationship with Jamie (and obvious aforementioned unrequited love).<br /> <br />Mostly, this is a well-written murder mystery set in London in 1557, in which the protagonist is a gay man in a world where that is completely taboo. LJG is asked to investigate the murder of a British soldier believed to be a spy (it’s the beginning of the Seven Years’ War, so that’s important). His investigation begins to coincide with his personal life in unexpected ways.<br /> <br />Gabaldon does that thing that Agatha Christie used to do where she has her ‘detective’ have long conversations with people, and the people are very well developed. Like Miss Marple and Hercule Poirot, LJG is an outsider, although he masquerades as a functional, normal member of society, hiding his ‘deviation’ from public view. But he feels it, and because he feels it, it colors all his interactions in this book, particularly those involving the seedier element of London life (including a trip to a whorehouse, and an all male gentleman’s club). It also makes him perfectly suited to rooting out the secrets other people keep.<br /> <br />My favorite mystery series are ones where they’re also secretly stealth character pieces, and this one certainly qualifies. It also has a wealth of side characters I enjoyed very much; even when they were unlikable, they were interesting. All in all, I’m really glad I picked this up. It was a nice palate cleanser after suffering through <i>The Fiery Cross</i> a couple of weeks ago, and it renewed my faith in Gabaldon as a writer. Can’t wait to read the rest of the series. (Get the audiobook if you can–narrator Jeff Woodman is always a good time.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2555064938604468369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1832000063" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1832000063" />
    <a title="Sophia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5063928-sophia"><img alt="Sophia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432187496p2/5063928.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1832000063?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia" href="/user/show/5063928-sophia">Sophia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/25392384-lord-john-and-the-private-matter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5063928-sophia?shelf=historical-mystery-suspense">historical-mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5063928-sophia?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1832000063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1248571568361846032">I read this book a couple years back and enjoyed stepping into the world of Lord John and his Georgian London. A cunning mystery and an opportunity to know John and those around him better made it a delightful read. <br/><br/>However, for this, my second encounter, I chose to experience the story on audio with new to me narrator, Jeff Woodman. I'm happy to report that this story was better than ever as a result. His storytelling was amazing and matched well with the characters, tone of the book, and sitat</span>
  <span id="freeText1248571568361846032" style="display:none">I read this book a couple years back and enjoyed stepping into the world of Lord John and his Georgian London. A cunning mystery and an opportunity to know John and those around him better made it a delightful read. <br /><br />However, for this, my second encounter, I chose to experience the story on audio with new to me narrator, Jeff Woodman. I'm happy to report that this story was better than ever as a result. His storytelling was amazing and matched well with the characters, tone of the book, and sitatuion.<br /><br />John's brother, Hal, the head of the household is gone and of course John stumbles across a situation that is a delicate family matter that he has no idea how to handle. Before he gets far with figuring this out, he is commissioned by the Army to investigate missing papers, a soldier's death, and the trail to the spymaster for whom the stolen papers were destined.<br /><br />John's investigation takes him to the seedier side of town, but also involves some powerful people. He carefully follows each lead and senses there is much more going on and people know a whole lot more than they are telling him. Slow, but sure he gets there and then he is confronted by yet another situation.<br /><br />It reads like a cozy mystery blended with historical fiction and has a gentle pacing. The story is parts character study and development and parts suspense. Loved getting to know Lord John better after encountering him in the Outlander series' Voyager. In fact, this is a spin-off and would fall after that in sequence.<br /><br />Definite recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1248571568361846032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1552539324" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1552539324" />
    <a title="Slip!" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31298776-slip"><img alt="Slip!" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564702906p2/31298776.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1552539324?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Slip!" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Slip!" href="/user/show/31298776-slip">Slip!</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31298776-slip?shelf=meh-wouuldnt-read-again">meh-wouuldnt-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31298776-slip?shelf=very-good-but-not-best">very-good-but-not-best</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1552539324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14664450050883421516">Ok, why why WHY does Gabaldon insist on ANOTHER plot of gay men?<br/>Ok, yes, that sort of thought and leanings were around back then. But here's the thing. Even covert, they weren't so open about it! I mean, back then, that sort of stance really wasn't all that common. And if it was, men (or woman) took the upmost care to conceal it, or be very careful about to whom they revealed it on. <br/><br/>I just think there is so much potential in this story, specifically to Grey, if it wasn't clouded by the sexual st</span>
  <span id="freeText14664450050883421516" style="display:none">Ok, why why WHY does Gabaldon insist on ANOTHER plot of gay men?<br />Ok, yes, that sort of thought and leanings were around back then. But here's the thing. Even covert, they weren't so open about it! I mean, back then, that sort of stance really wasn't all that common. And if it was, men (or woman) took the upmost care to conceal it, or be very careful about to whom they revealed it on. <br /><br />I just think there is so much potential in this story, specifically to Grey, if it wasn't clouded by the sexual stances that became a small plot line of its own. I mean, Randall was acceptable and enough for me. <br /><br />But TWO men who are in love with Jamie? Like, that's a pretty big cast of characters right there, for the time period. It was rather disappointing, actually. It took the intrigue of the character away, really. He became just another one, so to speak.<br /><br />I mean, Randall (god rest his soul, I <i>loved</i> him!!), was a character WITH the angle of having love for Jamie. But it wasn't because he was necessarily gay - it was because he was a malicious sadist who eventually fell in love with his victim after having a personal vendetta against Jamie. It is similar to Stockholm syndrome, if you will; captors can easily fall in love with their captive. <br /><br />And yeah, sure, Grey owed Jamie for sparing his life. But even as we learn the background of how he met up with Jamie again, and even in the fourth instillment, Drums of Autumn, we get more info of the interactions that had occurred betwixt the two. But its not the same, it just isn't!!<br /><br />It makes me wonder if Gabaldon was desperate to recreate what Jamie and Randall had. Whatever she was thinking, it didn't have the desired effect, I think. I feel like she wanted readers to feel pity or something for Grey because of what side of the tracks he stands on, and what it was for Jamie. But I really felt nothing. <br /><br />To be understood; I don't hate gay men or woman. <br /><br />I just hated GREY.<br /><br />So, one star for sort of ruining the whole thing for me because of that. But, two for the per usual, excellent descriptions and narrations. <br /><br />My favorite quote of the entire book had to be; "His lips were so pursed and white it reminded Grey of a dog's anus."</span>
  <a data-text-id="14664450050883421516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_300005629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300005629" />
    <a title="Erica Anderson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3676259-erica-anderson"><img alt="Erica Anderson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442486349p2/3676259.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300005629?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica Anderson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica Anderson" href="/user/show/3676259-erica-anderson">Erica Anderson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3676259-erica-anderson?shelf=historical-mystery">historical-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3676259-erica-anderson?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300005629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10077031833393001023">I know this borders on the heretical, but I've been enjoying the Lord John series <i>more</i> than <i>Outlander</i> proper. In contrast to the larger-than-life Jamie Fraser, Lord John Grey is relatively diffident and self-effacing. His homosexuality adds a profound dimension to his character. Because the books are short (at least in Gabaldonian terms), there are few tangents and minimal plot clutter, allowing John's character to shine without the overwhelming presence of Claire or Fraser. <br/><br/>Lord John is so very</span>
  <span id="freeText10077031833393001023" style="display:none">I know this borders on the heretical, but I've been enjoying the Lord John series <i>more</i> than <i>Outlander</i> proper. In contrast to the larger-than-life Jamie Fraser, Lord John Grey is relatively diffident and self-effacing. His homosexuality adds a profound dimension to his character. Because the books are short (at least in Gabaldonian terms), there are few tangents and minimal plot clutter, allowing John's character to shine without the overwhelming presence of Claire or Fraser. <br /><br />Lord John is so very <i>decent</i> that I find some sections of the book almost painful to read, a tribute to Gabaldon's ability to create sympathetic characters. The Lord John books should appeal not only to <i>Outlander</i> fans, but also to readers who like well-crafted historical mysteries. If you like C.S. Harris and Ashley Gardner, the Lord John books are an excellent bet. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10077031833393001023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_57114077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57114077" />
    <a title="Jojo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/118531-jojo"><img alt="Jojo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544403747p2/118531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/57114077?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jojo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jojo" href="/user/show/118531-jojo">Jojo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099461173" href="/book/show/864698.Lord_John_and_the_Private_Matter">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer57114077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17954676370356649327">I never would have picked this book up except that I am starved - starved, I say! - for English-language books here in Japan, and because I am so desperate for reading material, I will now read pretty much anything I can find that looks vaguely interesting, especially if it's cheap. This was on the ¥500 yen table at Tower Records, and looked like it was maybe not as crap as everything else offered for the same price. So I picked it up even though I have, like, negative interest in reading the Ou</span>
  <span id="freeText17954676370356649327" style="display:none">I never would have picked this book up except that I am starved - starved, I say! - for English-language books here in Japan, and because I am so desperate for reading material, I will now read pretty much anything I can find that looks vaguely interesting, especially if it's cheap. This was on the ¥500 yen table at Tower Records, and looked like it was maybe not as crap as everything else offered for the same price. So I picked it up even though I have, like, negative interest in reading the Outlander series that this is connected to (it's really long! and I kind of hate time travel!).<br /><br />Ended up really enjoying it! There were a few things not as fully explained as I would have liked (probably because I was expected to know them from reading the Outlander series), but for the most part the characters and writing and story worked for me. Still don't really want to read the Outlander books, but I do want to read more about Lord John.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17954676370356649327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8313237218913623745">I havent read anything else by Diana Gabaldon and I probably never will. When I read it, I didnt know much of the character's backstory - only that he had been a minor character in some other epic adventure. But it sounded intresting and as it turned out, it didnt dissapoint.<br/><br/>I picked it up because I wanted to read about a lead that was gay - it was part of the pride festival theme and one of my favourite bookstores had gathered a bunch of their books with homosexual lead characters as a tribute </span>
  <span id="freeText8313237218913623745" style="display:none">I havent read anything else by Diana Gabaldon and I probably never will. When I read it, I didnt know much of the character's backstory - only that he had been a minor character in some other epic adventure. But it sounded intresting and as it turned out, it didnt dissapoint.<br /><br />I picked it up because I wanted to read about a lead that was gay - it was part of the pride festival theme and one of my favourite bookstores had gathered a bunch of their books with homosexual lead characters as a tribute to the subject. As it was, I was rather careful because I didnt want something like a leads sexual orientation to take over the actual story of the book. The clerks assured me that yes, this would probably be the book for me and I have to agree with them, it is. <br /><br />For the actual story... well. Its not particulary complex but its witty and fast paced in a realistic sort of way.<br /><br />Its not a mindblowing super classic but its a good read and it works fine as a stand alone novel. The summary of the next book in this series didnt sound too intresting and neither did the "main" series but we'll see. Maybe in the future Ill pick up them too. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_3544725510" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3544725510" />
    <a title="Geordie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8609965-geordie"><img alt="Geordie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333644941p2/8609965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3544725510?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Geordie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Geordie" href="/user/show/8609965-geordie">Geordie</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3544725510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6452149198639295346">A mystery set in 18th century London, young Lord John must recover vital documents stolen from his regiment. Along the way he must deal with matters of family honor and the murders that crop up around these valuable papers.<br/><br/>This was a fun read, I definitely recommend it and hope to read the next in the series. The prose was good, and there was an intense, authentic feeling of place. Lord John was a likable, complex character, balancing the perils of being homosexual in his time, while never feeli</span>
  <span id="freeText6452149198639295346" style="display:none">A mystery set in 18th century London, young Lord John must recover vital documents stolen from his regiment. Along the way he must deal with matters of family honor and the murders that crop up around these valuable papers.<br /><br />This was a fun read, I definitely recommend it and hope to read the next in the series. The prose was good, and there was an intense, authentic feeling of place. Lord John was a likable, complex character, balancing the perils of being homosexual in his time, while never feeling any shame for it.<br /><br />I was happily surprised with how good the book was, but was disappointed with the ending. A German name is mentioned in the investigation, and a couple days afterwards Lord John decides abruptly (with no explanation) that he must find the person with that name immediately. The stolen papers are recovered, but all other matters of the case are not resolved satisfactorily at all <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the two murders are shrugged off because they happened to scumbags, Lord John almost dies from mercury poisoning, but the poisoner only meant to incapacitate him, so, all is forgiven? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> In the last chapter, Lord John slips and falls, knocking himself out for several hours. The accident and unconsciousness have NO connection to the story. I'm trying my best to figure out why the author put them in, they added nothing. Was that supposed to be a last minute bit of shock or peril, or did she just have no idea how to transition to the last scene? He was knocked out by complete accident, and for no (plot) reason at all.<br /><br />Overall this was fun to read. Please approach it as an espionage tale including murders (not my usual cup of tea, but again, I enjoyed this one); don't think of it as a murder story with some espionage, you'll be disappointed. And be braced for the ending to wrap things up unsatisfactorily. I look forward to the next in the series, just hope its climax is solider.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6452149198639295346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1879184460" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1879184460" />
    <a title="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out"><img alt="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473475487p2/16915869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1879184460?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" href="/user/show/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out">Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/25392384-lord-john-and-the-private-matter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=set-in-1700s">set-in-1700s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=outside-the-usa">outside-the-usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=military">military</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1879184460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2855048464155712653">I'm finally getting a chance to reread this series along with Voyager, and it's proving as fun as the first time around.<br/><br/>I can't believe I forgot about my precious Tom Byrd, the most put-upon footman in all of London. Hee! Lord John does have a tendency to destroy his suits beyond repair, but Tom tries. Too bad that it seems like Gabaldon hadn't created Tom Byrd until she started writing these novellas, since he's not in any of the Outlander books.<br/><br/>I did remember Captain Stephan von Namtzen, becau</span>
  <span id="freeText2855048464155712653" style="display:none">I'm finally getting a chance to reread this series along with Voyager, and it's proving as fun as the first time around.<br /><br />I can't believe I forgot about my precious Tom Byrd, the most put-upon footman in all of London. Hee! Lord John does have a tendency to destroy his suits beyond repair, but Tom tries. Too bad that it seems like Gabaldon hadn't created Tom Byrd until she started writing these novellas, since he's not in any of the Outlander books.<br /><br />I did remember Captain Stephan von Namtzen, because who could possibly forget the sexual tension between him and John? Not me! *fans self* I did however forget that he was in this book, so it was fun to meet him again much sooner than I'd counted on.<br /><br />And then there's Lord John, who has a rather delicate problem to deal with in regards to his cousin's betrothed and a murder to investigate for the Crown that keeps getting more entangled the more he looks into it. And since 1757 London is not a friendly place for the gays, he has to do all this while keeping his sexual orientation a secret - which is common practice on an average day but not so easy to do when his investigation takes him back to Lavender House. He's constantly walking a tight rope, and that rope just keeps getting tighter and more precarious. Since he refuses to marry just to keep up appearances, he is also lonely and unattached, and nursing the unrequited yen for Jaime Frasier. He's kind of a mess relationship-wise, honestly, but it's one of the things that is so intriguing about him, along with his pragmatism, empathy, strength and cunning.<br /><br />One of Gabaldon's many strengths is writing colorful and three-dimensional side characters, and there are many met here, my favorite being Nessie, the Scottish prostitute with a hate-on for English soldiers. Gabaldon's sense of time and place really shines through here as it does in her Outlander series. She gives us 18th century characters with 18th century sensibilities.<br /><br />The narrator, Jeff Woodman, does a great job. I can't say if all the accents are spot-on, but they sound pretty legit to my foreign ears, except maybe the Cornish accent for Trevelyan's was on the stilted side. Whether that's just the way he chose to speak his lines or he was having trouble with the accent, I don't know. He does a great job with voices, especially Tom Byrd's, and he gets all the emotional notes perfectly. I thought it would be hard to transition between Davina Porter, who does the Outlander books, to Jeff Woodman, but it wasn't at all. Both these series have real top-notch performers for their audiobooks, and they complement each other well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2855048464155712653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1038327147" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1038327147" />
    <a title="♥︎♥︎Sofia♥︎♥︎" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9317694-sofia"><img alt="♥︎♥︎Sofia♥︎♥︎" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414377707p2/9317694.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1038327147?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥︎♥︎Sofia♥︎♥︎" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥︎♥︎Sofia♥︎♥︎" href="/user/show/9317694-sofia">♥︎♥︎Sofia♥︎♥︎</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780440334521" href="/book/show/7036058-lord-john-and-the-private-matter">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1038327147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9447907328379937881">Nearing the end of my Outlander journey I realised, as I started An Echo in The Bone (#7) that there were things (and characters) alluded to within the first chapter that I was completely in the dark about. With trepidation I remembered warnings and a general consensus by other Outlander readers/fans that I should read The Lord John books before I reached this point but, honestly? I thought I'd be able to 'wing' it; I was wrong. With a screeching halt I had to temporarily abandon my love affair </span>
  <span id="freeText9447907328379937881" style="display:none">Nearing the end of my Outlander journey I realised, as I started An Echo in The Bone (#7) that there were things (and characters) alluded to within the first chapter that I was completely in the dark about. With trepidation I remembered warnings and a general consensus by other Outlander readers/fans that I should read The Lord John books before I reached this point but, honestly? I thought I'd be able to 'wing' it; I was wrong. With a screeching halt I had to temporarily abandon my love affair with Jamie Fraser to revert back to Lord John (a relatively important secondary character within the Outlander series) and the series of books written with him as the central focus; to say I was very, very unhappy about it is an understatement. <br /><br />Lord John Grey is not a character that I particularly care for within the series, in fact I'd go so far as to say I barely tolerate him. Barely. He is, for all intent and purpose, the "other woman' in this tale, and though his romantic feelings are not reciprocated by our hero (who has only ever loved our heroine. Aaahhhhh) everytime Lord John expresses his unrequited love? I kinda want to punch him in the face. You see how reading Lord John and The Private Matter might be a problem?<br /><br />And it was. The book is well written, Gabaldon's amazing literary talent shine through as always. Her characters were well rounded and the plot thoroughly thought-out and perfectly developed. And maybe if I had read them before Lord John became a feature in the Outlander story, I might have been more <i>sympatico,</i> but as it stood? I sat and 'gritted my teeth' throughout, and growled any time he mentioned Jamie Fraser and it was a hard, uphill battle to continue to the end (it's at time like this that my anti-flounce gene comes in handy) Finally I asked for help (thank you OBC!) and was advised that I didn't need to read all three novels and God knows how many novellas, I should read just the novels and, at a push, just the Lord John and the Brotherhood of the Blade in order to move on to Outlander book 7 and then come back to the rest later. I can say now, categorically, that that's <i>never</i> going to happen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9447907328379937881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_137327558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137327558" />
    <a title="Lisa Wolf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4103395-lisa-wolf"><img alt="Lisa Wolf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280855695p2/4103395.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10524652156740365257">Boy, I am so ambivalent over this book. I love the Outlander series, but was not enthralled with this first book featuring Lord John Grey. I liked the MC but the story itself I had a hard time getting into and the web got more convoluted as the story unfolded. Red herrings or truly are all the strings attached in a very mixed-up ball! It also highlighted the seamier side of late 18thC London life, not necessarily where I like to spend my time. So 2.5 stars.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1220214479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1220214479" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29515282-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550864214p2/29515282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1220214479?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/29515282-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29515282-nicole?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29515282-nicole?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29515282-nicole?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29515282-nicole?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1220214479&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1220214479" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer40669640318172469">While I'm still a fan of the character Lord John Grey, the absence of the lovable and magnificent Jamie and Claire highlights all of the weaknesses in Gabaldon's writing. Her characters are delightful - each one feels immediately familiar. But her writing is incredibly heavy-handed and in desperate need of a qualified editor. <br/><br/>The Lord John Grey novels, according to Gabaldon's website, were a chance for her to tell the story of this man who only appears briefly in the OUTLANDER series. Supposedly</span>
  <span id="freeText40669640318172469" style="display:none">While I'm still a fan of the character Lord John Grey, the absence of the lovable and magnificent Jamie and Claire highlights all of the weaknesses in Gabaldon's writing. Her characters are delightful - each one feels immediately familiar. But her writing is incredibly heavy-handed and in desperate need of a qualified editor. <br /><br />The Lord John Grey novels, according to Gabaldon's website, were a chance for her to tell the story of this man who only appears briefly in the OUTLANDER series. Supposedly rife with political intrigue and mystery, we are promised a deeper glimpse of a good man and soldier who has sacrificed much for God and country. I didn't feel I got that in this book. Political intrigue and mystery - maybe. It was certainly there, though her weaving of Lord John's "private matter" with the larger mystery at hand was inexpertly done, trite and extremely boring. I couldn't wait to finish just to put it behind me. <br /><br />But as for showing the other side of John Grey - I felt Gabaldon failed completely. (SPOILER?) We know from the OUTLANDER novels that Grey is a homosexual. It is his unrequited love for Jamie Fraser that endeared me to him and so I was looking forward to delving into his novels to learn more about the man. However, we learn hardly more beyond the fact that Lord John Grey is gay. In fact, she seems to remind us of his predilection every few pages, and - as with most of her writing - is not subtle in the least. I don't mean to say that I don't want to read about the sexual cravings of a gay man. I do - in fact. It's that - I happen to think Lord John Grey is the sum of many things. And that Gabaldon did him a great disservice in concentrating on just the one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="40669640318172469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_37238555" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37238555" />
    <a title="Marleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1616365-marleen"><img alt="Marleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576835511p2/1616365.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37238555?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marleen" href="/user/show/1616365-marleen">Marleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1616365-marleen?shelf=diana-gabaldon">diana-gabaldon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37238555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11608110056871045518">Ten years ago I devoured the first 4 books of the Outlander series, and then as sudden as the Outlander fever had taken me, it had also left me. I couldn’t get into the fifth book. I think I sort of got satiated with Jamie and Clare’s saga. Well they are hefty books, and I had to take a break from them. I haven’t started up since, but I will, soon, because I just adore Diana Gabaldon’s storytelling and I think that Jamie and Clare’s adventures are amazing and I’ve enjoyed them immensely.<br/>Lord Joh</span>
  <span id="freeText11608110056871045518" style="display:none">Ten years ago I devoured the first 4 books of the Outlander series, and then as sudden as the Outlander fever had taken me, it had also left me. I couldn’t get into the fifth book. I think I sort of got satiated with Jamie and Clare’s saga. Well they are hefty books, and I had to take a break from them. I haven’t started up since, but I will, soon, because I just adore Diana Gabaldon’s storytelling and I think that Jamie and Clare’s adventures are amazing and I’ve enjoyed them immensely.<br />Lord John and the Private Matter is the first spin-off featuring Lord John Grey, an English officer whom the readers are introduced to in the Outlanders books. I honestly don’t remember much of John Grey’s personality, except that he was a closeted gay character, who was decent to Jamie.<br />Here we discover a little bit more about Lord John and I’ve come to like him quite a bit. Overall the story-line of “the Private Matter” isn’t especially intricate or intriguing as I would’ve hoped, but it was interesting enough. What I enjoyed particularly was that the author absolutely succeeded into creating the atmosphere of 18th Century London, describing the life on the city streets in a captivating and authentic manner. I thought it was fascinating how she researched the gay subculture of time, e.g. Molly houses, the transvestites, the habits and customs of English society of the the time, without ever making it sound too vulgar or obnoxious.<br />I’ve also discovered that Lord Grey is a sensitive soul all wrapped up in a strong-willed and honourable man. I’m actually looking forward to reading the next books featuring this compelling (and decent) character.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11608110056871045518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_411904457" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/411904457" />
    <a title="Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/244706-elena"><img alt="Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1260219129p2/244706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/411904457?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena" href="/user/show/244706-elena">Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/244706-elena?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/244706-elena?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer411904457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1424868968260804005">Not entirely a success - this book is neither meaty, complex and id-pleasing (like Gabaldon's Outlander series) nor witty and smart (like a successful mystery novel), and ends up mediocre. <br/><br/>I think part of the problem here is that Gabaldon's strength is in the epic full of anguish, love, and sex, and this book has none of the first two, and the third is entirely off-stage. She's stuck in part due to the fact that Lord John Grey, the protagonist here, is a secondary character in the Outlander book</span>
  <span id="freeText1424868968260804005" style="display:none">Not entirely a success - this book is neither meaty, complex and id-pleasing (like Gabaldon's Outlander series) nor witty and smart (like a successful mystery novel), and ends up mediocre. <br /><br />I think part of the problem here is that Gabaldon's strength is in the epic full of anguish, love, and sex, and this book has none of the first two, and the third is entirely off-stage. She's stuck in part due to the fact that Lord John Grey, the protagonist here, is a secondary character in the Outlander books, and thus has much of his story pre-determined. Nothing too exciting can happen to him here, because it would undermine or undo those books.<br /><br />Another issue is that Gabaldon stumbles in her dealings with the queer subcultures of 18th century London. She raises interesting issues and introduces potentially interesting characters - and then drops them, with their stories unsettled. <br /><br />Lord John Grey himself, a highlight of the Outlander books, seems pale and cold here, close to boring. The best scene was his interaction with a Scottish whore halfway through the book. I think without the English-Scottish culture clash, Gabaldon can't manage to write compelling character interplay.<br /><br />It's not an awful book, but it was a disappointment. I guess if I want to see really interesting (and sexy) things happen to Lord John Grey, I'll have to rely on fanfiction. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1424868968260804005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2708760021" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2708760021" />
    <a title="D Dyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92934393-d-dyer"><img alt="D Dyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551830399p2/92934393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2708760021?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="D Dyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="D Dyer" href="/user/show/92934393-d-dyer">D Dyer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16001018855429973734">Reviewed after re-reading.<br/>I actually enjoyed this book more the second time I’ve read it than I did after my first read. That maybe because I am reading it this time around very closely after reading Voyager, the outlander book who’s events around this book chronologically speaking. That said, the outlander book and it’s characters are only occasionally and tangentially mentioned in this novel and you don’t have to have read those books to enjoy this one. Gabaldon shows a lot of skill here in pr</span>
  <span id="freeText16001018855429973734" style="display:none">Reviewed after re-reading.<br />I actually enjoyed this book more the second time I’ve read it than I did after my first read. That maybe because I am reading it this time around very closely after reading Voyager, the outlander book who’s events around this book chronologically speaking. That said, the outlander book and it’s characters are only occasionally and tangentially mentioned in this novel and you don’t have to have read those books to enjoy this one. Gabaldon shows a lot of skill here in presenting a deep and realistic historical novel with characters who feel both appropriate for their time and incredibly relatable. I absolutely love lord John Gray who struggles both with his queerness and with fulfilling the duties he feels are a part of his station and family.<br />This book is a mystery, John is tasked with discovering the identity of a spy, but it functions much more as a character study then it does a Holmesian puzzle. Most of the investigating comes in the form of long conversations, and getting to know these characters, some of whom come from the lowest classes and are distinctly outside of acceptable culture for this time, both presented through their own dialogue with John and through his perspective as an outsider who has managed to keep his separation from the dominant culture a secret, is absolutely fascinating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16001018855429973734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText3970364047333762421" style="display:none">Aw, I should probably give it three, but I love Lord John. I was severely dissappointed, however, with the pages upon pages where the "bad guys" just...told us what-all had been going on the whole time. It was done as well as such an info-dumping monstrosity could be done, with a bit of tension in the background and explanations for why they'd do this, and how it was all going down.<br /><br />But still.
